<div id="review_3251287263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3251287263" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3251287263?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781478934547" href="/book/show/26335236-baptism-of-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3251287263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2413646763229943322">This 3rd full-length novel about the witcher Geralt of Rivia has him very much injured from the events of the previous volume. At least at the start. Then he does what Geralt does best: he travels across the country on a mission. This time, however, he's not hunting a monster. Instead, he's looking for Ciri. Actually, he is told she's at the emperor's court in Nilfgaard so that is where he's going. We still don't know what's happened to Yennefer (initially) so it's just Geralt and Dandelion.<br/>Duri</span>
  <span id="freeText2413646763229943322" style="display:none">This 3rd full-length novel about the witcher Geralt of Rivia has him very much injured from the events of the previous volume. At least at the start. Then he does what Geralt does best: he travels across the country on a mission. This time, however, he's not hunting a monster. Instead, he's looking for Ciri. Actually, he is told she's at the emperor's court in Nilfgaard so that is where he's going. We still don't know what's happened to Yennefer (initially) so it's just Geralt and Dandelion.<br />During the quest through the country we soon find out that basically every city is burning. The coup from the previous book has turned into all-out war. There are lots of refugees and one group of them is accompanied (and protected) by a few dwarves. Geralt joins them and makes a few friends along the way. One of them being a very special one indeed (can't say that was a real mystery to me but it was still funny).<br />It turns out that a certain "Dark Knight" is following them, too - and not necessarily for the reason the reader and/or Geralt thinks.<br />And then there is Ciri's POV of which we get a few glimpses in between. Because - spoiler alert (not really) - she's not actually at the emperor's court.<br />And yes, eventually we even find out what has happened to Yennefer since Geralt saw her last (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a jade statuette ... that was interesting, but WHY it was done, of course, even more so <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br /><br />If you think anything is getting resolved here, you better think again. The machinations here are as wide-ranging and detailed as in LOTR and we didn't get a build-up of 2 books only to have it resolved willy-nilly. And that is only just. <br /><br />Despite the grimness, I loved to see the world-wide repercussions of the conflict broiling over. Yes, it was hard to read about people eating rotting horse corpses because that is a feast compared to what they've had for months. Yes, seeing practically the entire world burn was uncomfortable. Then again, I loved the OLD world most, the one with all the monsters and critters - and since those had been driven to or near extinction, I didn't care too much about the humans. *lol* <br />I was here for the magic. Because this conflict is also about magic vs. politics of "normal" humans. And, within the circle of magic-users, the powers truggle of the different factions (there are more than the ones we were previously familiar with).<br /><br />I liked the set-up, I liked the further build-up, most noteably also via Ciri's POV and her personal development. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew she wouldn't stay Geralt's little girl forever and am curious if she'll become truly rotten (she already kinda is) / the big bad indeed or if / how easily Geralt can get her back on the right track. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The writing has remained as good as in the previous books, the character building remains wonderful as well. Knowing that all MCs are fighting hard to get back to one another (some more than others) tucked at my heartstrings. Nevertheless, this was the least fun so far. Maybe I'm just too impatient? *lol*<br />Anyway, great fun so I'm not really allowed to complain. Like, at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2413646763229943322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_312148828" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Fadi Antwan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73433375-fadi-antwan"><img alt="Fadi Antwan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565752882p2/73433375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2974864142?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fadi Antwan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fadi Antwan" href="/user/show/73433375-fadi-antwan">Fadi Antwan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316219181" href="/book/show/18656031-baptism-of-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2974864142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer138952229617779710"><b>4.5/5</b><br/><br/>I have to say, the main saga, at least when it comes to the last two books, is no joke. It requires <b>a lot</b> of attention, so consider yourselves warned. So many characters have been introduced over the last two books, it's hard to keep track of who's who sometimes. and rarely is important information given explicitly. I had make deductions and read some passages over and over again to make sure I really understood what happened. I'm fairly certain it's not the translation, just the author's w</span>
  <span id="freeText138952229617779710" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5</b><br /><br />I have to say, the main saga, at least when it comes to the last two books, is no joke. It requires <b>a lot</b> of attention, so consider yourselves warned. So many characters have been introduced over the last two books, it's hard to keep track of who's who sometimes. and rarely is important information given explicitly. I had make deductions and read some passages over and over again to make sure I really understood what happened. I'm fairly certain it's not the translation, just the author's writing style. Anyway, that's not why I took off a star from my rating. I actually enjoy the ambiguity, which is not unique to this installment–the plot is simply more complex here. I still loved this volume, but I'm missing the emotional connection that I felt with the first three books in the series, probably since the main characters have been separated for quite some time now. I'm really enjoying the political plot though, and I love the new side characters, so still going strong!</span>
  <a data-text-id="138952229617779710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3017636274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3017636274" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3017636274?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/51194434-baptism-of-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3017636274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11356922524699073850">Lots of plot development in this installment as we find Geralt forming a fellowship of misfits (including Zoltan!) in his quest to rescue Ciri. The plot is very Witcher focused here, with little deviation into what our other heroes are doing, which meant we got a lot more character development between Dandelion, Geralt and everyone else. It was nice to see how the plot is finally coming together after such a slow burn. We do also still get glimpses of what Yennefer and Ciri are up to, just so th</span>
  <span id="freeText11356922524699073850" style="display:none">Lots of plot development in this installment as we find Geralt forming a fellowship of misfits (including Zoltan!) in his quest to rescue Ciri. The plot is very Witcher focused here, with little deviation into what our other heroes are doing, which meant we got a lot more character development between Dandelion, Geralt and everyone else. It was nice to see how the plot is finally coming together after such a slow burn. We do also still get glimpses of what Yennefer and Ciri are up to, just so they aren't forgotten, and in the case of Ciri her character has taken a dark turn, but this feels very firmly like Geralt's story. <br /><br />The plot itself is still political, full of war talk and strategic planning, but its the subtle smattering of humour throughout that keeps this entertaining. The witch trial in particular stands out for its comedy moments, as well as just about anything Zoltan says. Geralt's band of merry men (and woman) are also a really good combination of characters with their own murky pasts and foibles.<br /><br />The plot progression also means that by the end it feels like we are finally getting somewhere. We have a plan, we have some answers in terms of Ciri's mysterious powers (although not going to lie it was a little complicated to wrap my head around) and there's a light at the end of the endless dark tunnel.<br /><br />I do love the Witcher world. Its feels incredibly intricate and well thought out with characters that I've grown to love. They're a welcome relief during the current climate. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11356922524699073850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1057480627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1057480627" />
    <a title="Kaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15462098-kaya"><img alt="Kaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485382914p2/15462098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1057480627?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaya" href="/user/show/15462098-kaya">Kaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316219181" href="/book/show/18656031-baptism-of-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1057480627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1503356189294145720"><b>
  <i>“Since when did you know anything about mimicking bird calls, Zoltan?’ ‘That’s the whole point. If you hear a strange, unrecognizable sound, you’ll know it’s me.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>This book is the strongest one when you consider the character development so far, but the weakest one if you have in mind the plot and action. All our main characters are departed and looking for each other while simultaneously hiding from the common enemy. After a while, it becomes repetitive they have no idea what to do with thei</span>
  <span id="freeText1503356189294145720" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Since when did you know anything about mimicking bird calls, Zoltan?’ ‘That’s the whole point. If you hear a strange, unrecognizable sound, you’ll know it’s me.”</i>
</b><br /><br />This book is the strongest one when you consider the character development so far, but the weakest one if you have in mind the plot and action. All our main characters are departed and looking for each other while simultaneously hiding from the common enemy. After a while, it becomes repetitive they have no idea what to do with their lives. <br /><br />We follow Geralt at his journey to Nilfgaard to save Ciri. He joins forces with Milva, a half-Dryad, Dandelion, who always finds his way to be nearby, a group of dwarves, my favourite Regis and a Nilfgaardian, who claims he’s not a Nilfgaardian, named Cahir. They have a wonderful time together and mostly of their scenes I spent laughing my head off, but besides that, the plot has nothing to offer. <br /><br />The main downfall is that the plot just falls flat and the reader keeps waiting for something huge to happen but it rarely does. Only on a few pages happens something truly significant for the future destinies of our main characters. While that one plot twist is really exciting and totally caught me off guard, I still long for the action-packed story from the first two books. <br /><br /><i>“<b>Were</b> I to attempt to be good to everyone, to the entire world and to all the creatures living in it, it would be a drop of fresh water in the salt sea. In other words, a wasted effort. Thus, I decided to do specific good; good which would not go to waste. I’m good to myself and my immediate circle.”</i><br /><br />The dwarves have particularly interesting point of view. <br /><br /><i>“Your talk's so clever it makes my head spin,' Milva snorted. 'And all your wisdom comes down to what's under a woman's skirt. Woeful philosophers.”</i><br /><br />Milva had some amazing comebacks and was such an awesome contrast to quiet Geralt.<br /> <br />Geralt is moody and even more stubborn than usual . What’s even worse, he has become boring. Yes, he had a few hilarious one liners, but besides that, he got so much screen time and through all of it he was constantly broody and ready to fight. I couldn’t understand why they even stayed with him when he was so obnoxious.<br /><br /><i>“What a company I ended up with,’ Geralt continued, shaking his head. ‘Brothers in arms! A team of heroes! What have I done to deserve it? A poetaster with a lute. A wild and lippy half-dryad, half-woman. A vampire, who’s about to notch up his fifth century. And a bloody Nilfgaardian who insists he isn’t a Nilfgaardian.”</i><br /><br />This was one of his rare funny moments. <br /><br />I hate what’s being done to Ciri. Before this book, she was the heart of the plot and know she’s a sad shell of who she used to be. I just can’t understand the point of her role in the gang. What is she supposed to learn from that experience? Because to me it just looks like another filler that keeps her and Geralt apart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1503356189294145720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3214455074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3214455074" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89114120-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542580543p2/89114120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3214455074?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/89114120-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18924205-baptism-of-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89114120-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3214455074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11251313319016201803">Spoiler-free review, you can read this even if you haven‘t read the previous books. <br/><br/><br/>This series is so unique. It took me a while to get into it but I‘m so glad I didn‘t give up on it. The world, the themes, the characters all really grew to me.<br/><br/>In Baptism of Fire you get a lot of Geralt. We follow him and his companions (who are all amazing characters by the way) on their journey through the war torn land to find Ciri. I loved the group dynamics and how disturbing war is portrayed and how we expi</span>
  <span id="freeText11251313319016201803" style="display:none">Spoiler-free review, you can read this even if you haven‘t read the previous books. <br /><br /><br />This series is so unique. It took me a while to get into it but I‘m so glad I didn‘t give up on it. The world, the themes, the characters all really grew to me.<br /><br />In Baptism of Fire you get a lot of Geralt. We follow him and his companions (who are all amazing characters by the way) on their journey through the war torn land to find Ciri. I loved the group dynamics and how disturbing war is portrayed and how we expierience it through characters who are not directly involved in the war.<br /><br /> I missed Yen and Ciri a bit but it was nice to spend more time with Geralt after he was a little bit absent in the last two books. His development in this installment is incredibly well done. I especially liked how he started opening up and stopped being all like „I don‘t need anybody“ it was kind of touching to be honest. <br /><br />We get to spend a little bit time with Yen (not enough though), the scene with her was really well done and we also finally learn more about Ciri‘s blood line. <br /><br />This series doesn‘t have crazy plot twists, but instead interesting reveals, it has a lot of philosophical talk and amazing action sprinkled in. There is no good and evil, every character makes mistakes and tries to make up for them. Every race shows signs of cruelty and kindness. If you are in the mood for something different and that sounds like something you might like I highly recommend these books (even though I wasn‘t the biggest fan of the first three books).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11251313319016201803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6pCfpfuXOzxF6YRkWvGhSLLOsS+VRkw0Y9/wN0b/FbszIbgfuSOf5uWSxSSGCbOBCGWCaoqZlwrpF5zOEG96oA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l1GNfVM5Bnc9j2tU+I2HRlyhlzMhVDDzc6ARFHYcrIZO4KrHEY2irZ30KhQkdZWP5gqkdj6L6835aH3tIIzDnQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski">About Andrzej Sapkowski</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1241014902p3/38569.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski">Andrzej Sapkowski
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
11,109
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4892691394350148552">Andrzej Sapkowski, born June 21, 1948 in Łódź, is a Polish fantasy writer. Sapkowski studied economics, and before turning to writing, he had worked as a senior sales representative for a foreign trade company. His first short story, The Witcher (Wiedźmin), was published in Fantastyka, Poland's leading fantasy literary magazine, in 1986 and was enormously successful both with readers and critics. </span>
  <span id="freeText4892691394350148552" style="display:none">Andrzej Sapkowski, born June 21, 1948 in Łódź, is a Polish fantasy writer. Sapkowski studied economics, and before turning to writing, he had worked as a senior sales representative for a foreign trade company. His first short story, The Witcher (Wiedźmin), was published in Fantastyka, Poland's leading fantasy literary magazine, in 1986 and was enormously successful both with readers and critics. Sapkowski has created a cycle of tales based on the world of The Witcher, comprising three collections of short stories and five novels. This cycle and his many other works have made him one of the best-known fantasy authors in Poland in the 1990s.<br /><br />The main character of The Witcher (alternative translation: The Hexer) is Geralt, a mutant assassin who has been trained since childhood to hunt down and destroy monsters. Geralt exists in an ambiguous moral universe, yet manages to maintain his own coherent code of ethics. At the same time cynical and noble, Geralt has been compared to Raymond Chandler's signature character Philip Marlowe. The world in which these adventures take place is heavily influenced by Slavic mythology.<br /><br />Sapkowski has won five Zajdel Awards, including three for short stories "Mniejsze zło" (Lesser Evil) (1990), "Miecz przeznaczenia" (Sword of Destiny) (1992) and "W leju po bombie" (In a Bomb Crater) (1993), and two for the novels "Krew elfów" (Blood of Elves) (1994) and "Narrenturm" (2002). He also won the Spanish Ignotus Award, best anthology, for The Last Wish in 2003, and for "Muzykanci" (The Musicians), best foreign short story, same year.<br /><br />In 1997, Sapkowski won the prestigious Polityka's Passport award, which is awarded annually to artists who have strong prospects for international success.<br /><br />In 2001, a Television Series based on the Witcher cycle was released in Poland and internationally, entitled Wiedźmin (The Hexer). A film by the same title was compiled from excerpts of the television series but both have been critical and box office failures.<br /><br />Sapkowski's books have been translated into Czech, Russian, Lithuanian, German, Spanish, French, Ukrainian, and Portuguese. An English translation of The Last Wish short story collection was published by Gollancz in 2007.<br /><br />The Polish game publisher, CD Projekt, created a role-playing PC game based on this universe, called The Witcher, which was released in October 2007. There is also a mobile version of the game which has been created by Breakpoint Games and is being published by Hands-On Mobile in Western Europe,Latin America and Asia Pacific.<br /><br />The English translation of Sapkowski's novel Blood of Elves won the David Gemmell Legends Award in 2009.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4892691394350148552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
